President crashes the market by shutting down COVID relief talks - during a storm of tweets from White House quarantine attacking the FDA, FBI and Joe Biden</h2><ul class="mol-bullets-with-font"><li class="class"><strong>Trump went on a Twitter frenzy on Tuesday night firing off tweets while quarantined at the White House</strong></li><li class="class"><strong>Said he would sign a stand-alone bill for individual stimulus checks if legislation was passed</strong></li><li class="class"><b>Claimed he had ordered declassification of all Russian\xc2\xa0collusion probe documents</b></li><li class="class"><b>Slammed Fox News Anchor Chris Wallace over his debate moderation last week</b></li><li class="class"><b>Claimed confirmation of Judge Amy Coney Barrett to SCOTUS will be \'fast and easy\'\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0</b></li><li class="class"><b>It followed Trump\'s tweet that tanked the stock market by saying stimulus deal is off\xc2\xa0</b></li><li class="class"><b>Some have wondered if Trump is experiencing side effects of steroid treatment\xc2\xa0</b></li><li class="class"><b>Doctors say steroid\xc2\xa0dexamethasone can have side affects including aggression, agitation and confusion\xc2\xa0</b></li><li class="class"><b>Biden responded to the tirade by tweeting a gif saying \'get off Twitter\' pleading \'Please.\'\xc2\xa0</b></li></ul><p class="author-section byline-plain">By <a href="/home/search.html?s=&amp;authornamef=Keith+Griffith+For+Dailymail.com" class="author" rel="nofollow">Keith Griffith For Dailymail.com</a> </p><p class="byline-section"><span interesting-family-major-Chinese-firm.html%3Fito%3Demail_share_article-top_most-read-articles%0A%0A"> <!-- ad: https://mads.dailymail.co.uk/v6/us/news/none/article/other/leader_wide.html --><div class="adHolder" id="leader_wide"><script>adverts.addToArray({"pos":"leader_wide"})</script><span class="mol-ads-label-container"><span class="mol-ads-label">Advertisement</span></span></div> <p></p><div itemprop="articleBody"><p class="mol-para-with-font">President <a style="font-weight: bold;" href="/news/donald_trump/index.html" id="mol-3fa4d120-083f-11eb-9eb0-81bb4c8df1be">Donald Trump</a>\xc2\xa0has issued a flurry of 42 tweets and retweets on a wide range of topics in just a few hours while under quarantine in the East Wing, slamming the FBI, FDA, Joe Biden, House Speaker Nancy Pelosi and Chris Wallace.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">In one tweet, Trump set his terms for approving a stimulus bill from Congress, hours after saying he would cease all negotiations with Democrats until after the November 3 election.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">\'If I am sent a Stand Alone Bill for Stimulus Checks ($1,200), they will go out to our great people IMMEDIATELY. I am ready to sign right now. Are you listening Nancy?\' he tweeted on Tuesday night.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Trump has long called for individual stimulus payments and the continuation of the Paycheck Protection Program for small businesses, but has rejected other elements of the Democrats\' proposed stimulus plan. He reiterated that position on Tuesday.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">His barrage of tweets came shortly after the President was discharged from hospital mid-way through his treatment for Covid-19, which has him receiving a course of the steroid dexamethasone. Experts say the drug can cause mental side effects that \'have an impact on your thinking\' and could affect Mr Trump\'s brain.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">One medic said they see \'substantial\' side effects in around a third of people, including anxiety and aggression, while the class of medicines that the drug belongs to has in the past been found to impair judgement or even to cause psychosis.\xc2\xa0</p><div class="mol-img-group xwArtSplitter" style="style"> <div class="mol-img"> <div class="image-wrap"> <img id="i-ede34486dc2f4736" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7" data-src="https://i.dailymail.co.uk/1s/2020/10/07/06/34078374-8813057-Trump_is_seen_at_the_White_House_on_Monday_night_He_went_on_a_Tw-a-39_1602048578781.jpg" height="631" width="962" alt="Trump is seen at the White House on Monday night. </ul> </div> \n       \n            \n                <div class="fb">\n                  <h2>Share this article</h2>\n                  <div class="share"><span class="wai">Share</span></div>\n                </div>\n            \n   </div> </div><p class="mol-para-with-font">\'The House &amp; Senate should IMMEDIATELY Approve 25 Billion Dollars for Airline Payroll Support, &amp; 135 Billion Dollars for Paycheck Protection Program for Small Business,\' Mr Trump wrote in another tweet.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">\'Both of these will be fully paid for with unused funds from the Cares Act. Have this money. I will sign now!\' he continued.\xc2\xa0</p><div class="art-ins mol-factbox news halfRHS" data-version="2" id="mol-8406fef0-087c-11eb-a500-4160a3f8a3e6" data-permabox-url="https://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-8813057/Trump-calls-FDA-vaccine-delay-hit-job-flurry-tweets.html"> <h3 class="mol-factbox-title">COVID THERAPY DEXAMETHASONE CAUSES \'ADVERSE PSYCHIATRIC EFFECTS\'</h3> <div class="ins cleared mol-factbox-body"> <p class="mol-para-with-font">The President\'s barrage of tweets came just hours after he\xc2\xa0was discharged from hospital mid-way through his treatment for Covid-19, which has him receiving a course of the steroid dexamethasone. Experts say the drug can cause mental side effects that \'have an impact on your thinking\' and could affect Mr Trump\'s brain.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">One medic said they see \'substantial\' side effects in around a third of people, including anxiety and aggression, while the class of medicines that the drug belongs to has in the past been found to impair judgement or even to cause psychosis.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Speaker of the House of Representatives Nancy Pelosi suggested Trump may have warped thinking because of the steroids and said: \'There are people who think that steroids have an impact on your thinking. So, I don\'t know,\' Pelosi said, according to <a style="font-weight: bold;" class="class" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener" target="_blank" href="https://www.politico.com/news/2020/10/06/trump-ends-coronavirus-relief-talks-amid-stalemate-with-pelosi-426819">Politico</a>.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Doctors on Tuesday warned that dexamethasone comes with risks of serious side effects, including mood swings, aggression and confusion.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Trump\'s medical team on Sunday said the president was started on dexamethasone, a generic steroid long and widely used to reduce inflammation associated with other diseases. The steroid was begun after Trump experienced low oxygen levels.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Dr Ashish Jha,\xc2\xa0Dean of Brown University\'s School of Public Health,\xc2\xa0 told\xc2\xa0<a style="font-weight: bold;" class="class" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener" target="_blank" href="https://www.rawstory.com/2020/10/fox-news-doctor-says-hes-concerned-trump-could-be-experiencing-roid-rage/?utm_source=push_notifications">Fox News</a>: \'We definitely see in 30-40 percent of people pretty substantial effects...[of] the anxiety, the agitation.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Scientific <a style="font-weight: bold;" class="class" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener" target="_blank" href="https://www.mayoclinicproceedings.org/article/S0025-6196(11)61160-9/fulltext">r</a><a style="font-weight: bold;" class="class" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener" target="_blank" href="https://www.mayoclinicproceedings.org/article/S0025-6196(11)61160-9/fulltext">esearch </a>has shown that just a few days on dexamethasone can leave patients with memory and cognitive deficits. Corticosteroids - the class of drugs dexamethasone belongs to - may cause psychiatric side effects in anywhere from 1.8 to 57 percent of patients taking them.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">A study published by the Mayo Clinic in Minnesota found that unpredictable \'adverse psychiatric reactions\' were relatively common among people taking the drugs.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Experts\' first worry was that the use of dexamethasone to treat Trump suggested he was very sick, since the $6 steroid may be dangerous to people with mild COVID-19.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">But because it\'s been linked to everything from mania to memory problems, and aggression to psychosis, some are also concerned that the president\'s judgement could be impaired as he reportedly continues to work through his illness.</p></div><div data-swipe-article="false">\n<div class="adHolder mpu" id="mpu_factbox_1"><!- - ad: https://mads.dailymail.co.uk/v6/us/news/none/article/other/mpu_factbox.html - -><script>adverts.addToArray({"pos":"mpu_factbox"})</script><span class="mol-ads-label-container"><span class="mol-ads-label">Advertisement</span></span>\n</div>\n</div> </div><p class="mol-para-with-font">Biden, Trump\'s Democrat opponent in the presidential election, responded by tweeting a gif that could only be aimed at the president, of himself saying \'get off Twitter.\'</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Trump also reacted with displeasure to new FDA rules that will make it impossible for a vaccine to gain approval for release prior to the election.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">\'New FDA Rules make it more difficult for them to speed up vaccines for approval before Election Day. Just another political hit job!,\'\xc2\xa0Trump tweeted separately.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Earlier in the day,\xc2\xa0the FDA said vaccine makers should follow trial participants for at least two months to rule out any major side effects before seeking emergency approval - a timeline that will rule out any hope of a vaccine before the November 3 election, as Trump had often promised.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Other targets of the president\'s ire included House Speaker Nancy Pelosi and Fox News anchor Chris Wallace.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">\'Wear your mask in the \xe2\x80\x9cbeauty\xe2\x80\x9d parlor, Nancy!\' he said of Pelosi, in reference to surveillance footage that captured her visiting a San Francisco salon without a face covering, in violation of the city\'s lockdown rules.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">\'Chris Wallace was a total JOKE. Protected Joe all night long. He\xe2\x80\x99s no Mike!!!\' Trump tweeted of the newsman who moderated last week\'s presidential debates, comparing him unfavorably to his father Mike Wallace.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Mr Trump\'s tweets come as he is still taking the steroid dexamethasone as part of his treatment for coronavirus. The steroid is known to have side effects that can affect the brain and thought processes.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Speaker of the House of Representatives Nancy Pelosi suggested Trump may have warped thinking because of the steroids and said: \'There are people who think that steroids have an impact on your thinking. So, I don\'t know,\' Pelosi said, according to <a style="font-weight: bold;" class="class" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener" target="_blank" href="https://www.politico.com/news/2020/10/06/trump-ends-coronavirus-relief-talks-amid-stalemate-with-pelosi-426819">Politico</a>.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Doctors on Tuesday warned that dexamethasone comes with risks of serious side effects, including mood swings, aggression and confusion.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Trump\'s medical team on Sunday said the president was started on dexamethasone, a generic steroid long and widely used to reduce inflammation associated with other diseases. The steroid was begun after Trump experienced low oxygen levels.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Dr Ashish Jha,\xc2\xa0Dean of Brown University\'s School of Public Health,\xc2\xa0 told\xc2\xa0<a style="font-weight: bold;" class="class" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener" target="_blank" href="https://www.rawstory.com/2020/10/fox-news-doctor-says-hes-concerned-trump-could-be-experiencing-roid-rage/?utm_source=push_notifications">Fox News</a>: \'We definitely see in 30-40 percent of people pretty substantial effects...[of] the anxiety, the agitation.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Scientific <a style="font-weight: bold;" class="class" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener" target="_blank" href="https://www.mayoclinicproceedings.org/article/S0025-6196(11)61160-9/fulltext">r</a><a style="font-weight: bold;" class="class" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener" target="_blank" href="https://www.mayoclinicproceedings.org/article/S0025-6196(11)61160-9/fulltext">esearch </a>has shown that just a few days on dexamethasone can leave patients with memory and cognitive deficits. Corticosteroids - the class of drugs dexamethasone belongs to - may cause psychiatric side effects in anywhere from 1.8 to 57 percent of patients taking them.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">A study published by the Mayo Clinic in Minnesota found that unpredictable \'adverse psychiatric reactions\' were relatively common among people taking the drugs.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Experts\' first worry was that the use of dexamethasone to treat Trump suggested he was very sick, since the $6 steroid may be dangerous to people with mild COVID-19.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">But because it\'s been linked to everything from mania to memory problems, and aggression to psychosis, some are also concerned that the president\'s judgement could be impaired as he reportedly continues to work through his illness.\xc2\xa0</p><div class="moduleFull mol-video"><div><div itemprop="video" itemscope="itemscope"   "updateStyleOnHover": true\n      });\n  });\n  </script> </div> </div> </div></div></div><p class="mol-para-with-font">Trump\'s tweetstorm on Tuesday night followed an earlier tweet that sent stock markets crashing, when he said there would be no deal with Democrats on additional pandemic stimulus until after the election.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">While some theorized that it might be a negotiation tactic, others pointed to one of the medications Trump is taking to treat coronavirus,\xc2\xa0Dexamethasone, a steroid that can have side affects of aggression, agitation and confusion.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">On Monday, Trump\'s Twitter account was locked after he shared the email address of a New York Post columnist.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Twitter forced Trump to delete the tweet before unlocking the account, citing rules against sharing private information without consent.\xc2\xa0</p><mol-permabox id="mol-2a4d83d0-0849-11eb-9eb0-81bb4c8df1be"><div class=" mol-factbox news art-ins" data-version="2" id="mol-bf5ec4a0-074c-11eb-add8-dba3a484eb3b" data-permabox-url="/health/fb-8811739/WHAT-DRUGS-TRUMP-TREATED-WITH.html"><h3 class="mol-factbox-title">WHAT ARE THE DRUGS TRUMP IS BEING TREATED WITH AND WHAT ARE THEIR SIDE EFFECTS?</h3><div class="ins cleared mol-factbox-body"><p class="mol-para-with-font">President Trump has been given at least three potent drugs since announcing he tested positive for COVID-19 on Thursday night: Regeneron\'s cocktail of lab-made antibodies, the antiviral remdesivir, and the steroid dexamethasone.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Two of those medications are still experimental for treating COVID-19, and have given emergency use authorization by the Food and Drug Administration (FDA).\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">And White House physician Dr Sean Conley admitted on Monday that he would not disclose every single medication that the president is currently receiving (citing HIPAA patient privacy laws, which suggests that Trump himself gave Dr Conley permission to disclose some of his medications, but not all of them).\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Remdesivir, dexamethasone and the antibody cocktail are all in ongoing trials - but it\'s unclear if anyone besides the US Commander-in-Chief has ever been treated with all three.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Those three drugs are \'as much as we know [about the president\'s treatment regimen] - but I found it all really confusing, based on the reports,\' Dr Mark Poznansky, an infectious disease specialist at Massachusetts General Hospital told DailyMail.com.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">When asked if there was any precedent for treating a COVID-19 patient with all three drugs, Dr Poznansky replied, \'no.\'\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">\'But the individual decisions are based on the individual patient, and all bets are off when you\'re dealing with the president, the commander-in chief,\' he added.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">\'The implication is that the doctors believe that the risk of using these is outweighed by the potential benefit.\'\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">And while we have some clarity on the potential side effects of each of the\xc2\xa0 drugs, how they might interact is a mystery, \'because they just haven\'t been used frequently enough...we don\'t know about the combination,\' Dr Poznansky said.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">But even on their own, the side effects of these drugs could be particularly concerning for the president, considering that the steroid can cause mood swings, confusion and aggression.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">The drugs he was treated with and their potential side effects are:\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-bold mol-style-medium health-ccox">REGENERON\'S EXPERIMENTAL ANTIBODY COCKTAIL DRUG</span></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-bold">WHEN HE GOT IT:</span> Trump received a single 8 gram dose of Regeneron\'s cocktail of lab-made antibodies on Friday.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-bold">WHAT IT DOES:</span>\xc2\xa0REGN-COV2 is a combination of two lab-made versions of antibodies that help block the coronavirus from entering cells.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">One of the antibodies in the \'cocktail\' is based on an antibody that mice produce in response to coronavirus, while the other is based on an antibody isolated from the one of the first US COVID-19 patients.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">The hope is that the treatment drives down viral load, keeping it from overrunning the body and sending the immune system haywire, and preventing the infection from becoming severe.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-bold">WHAT THE DATA SAYS</span>: REGN-COV2 is still in early trial phases, but the first data from its clinical trial found that it dramatically lowered viral load within a week and cut recovery time in half in patients that weren\'t sick enough to be hospitalized.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Regeneron has not yet studied the drug in severely ill patients.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-bold">THE POSSIBLE SIDE EFFECTS</span>: The main concern is these types of treatment occasionally trigger \'antibody-dependent enhancement,\' which means the intended therapeutic actually helps the virus invade cells.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">So far, the trials don\'t suggest that REGN-COV2 is causing this phenomenon.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Antibody treatments can also cause allergic reactions including anaphylaxis, as well as fever, chills, nausea, diarrhea, weakness, headache and low blood pressure.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-medium health-ccox mol-style-bold">REMDESIVIR, GILEAD\'S ANTIVIRAL DRUG\xc2\xa0</span></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-bold">WHEN HE GOT IT: </span>President Trump was given his first dose of a five-day treatment course on Friday evening, after he was transferred from the White House to Walter Reed National Medical Center.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">He has since received his second and third dose of the drug.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-bold">WHAT IT DOES:</span> Remdesivir is an antiviral therapy originally designed to treat Ebola.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Scientists are not entirely sure why, but it helps to prevent coronavirus from making more copies of itself.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-bold">WHAT THE DATA SAYS:</span> Late-stage clinical trials of remdesivir found that patients treated with the drug were more likely to recover within 11 days than those who did not get the drug.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Their survival odds were about 40 percent better. In May, the drug became the first to get emergency use authorization from the FDA for treating severely ill patients. That approval has since been expanded to any hospitalized patients.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-bold">THE POSSIBLE SIDE EFFECTS:</span> It can cause nausea, vomiting, chils, sweating or light-headedness. The drug also may harm liver function, meaning that patients have to be closely monitored.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">There was some suggestion the Trump\'s liver and kidney function were suboptimal last night, but Dr Conley said Monday the president was just \'dehydrated.\'\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-medium health-ccox mol-style-bold">DEXAMETHASONE, THE $6 STEROID WITH COMMON PSYCHIATRIC SIDE EFFECTS</span></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-bold">WHEN HE GOT IT</span>: The president got a dose of dexamethasone on Saturday after he developed a high fever and his blood oxygen levels dropped below 94 percent on two occasions.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-bold">WHAT IT DOES:</span> Dexamethasone is a cheap steroid known to tamp down inflammation. It\'s already approved for use in other conditions in the US.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-bold">WHAT THE DATA SAYS: </span>Although it hasn\'t yet been given emergency approval in the US, dexamethasone is the most promising treatment yet for coronavirus.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">In a major UK study, the steroid cut the risk of death by 36 percent for patients sick enough to need breathing machines and\xc2\xa0<span style="font-size: 16px;">by 18 percent for patients needing just supplemental oxygen.\xc2\xa0</span></p><p class="mol-para-with-font">However, it seemed harmful at earlier stages or milder cases of illness: 18 percent of those on the drug died versus 14 percent of those given usual care.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">For that reason, many doctors were alarmed to see President Trump treated with the drug because using it suggested either that he was very sick, or that doctors were taking a risk in giving it to him early.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-bold">THE POSSIBLE SIDE EFFECTS:</span>\xc2\xa0 The steroid is potent, and can cause swelling, headaches, stomach pain, nausea, weakness, dizziness sleep problems, vision changes, skin problems, severe allergic reactions including mood changes.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">These mood changes include aggression, agitation and confusion.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">\'Steroids are always very dangerous medications to use,\' Dr Edward Jones-Lopez, an infectious disease specialist at the University of Southern California in Los Angeles, told Reuters.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">\'That is why it (dexamethasone) is used in severe to critical patients... There can be neuropsychiatric side effects. These are medications that we use very, very carefully.\'\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font"></p></div><div data-swipe-article="false">\n<div class="adHolder mpu" id="mpu_factbox_2"><!- - ad: https://mads.dailymail.co.uk/v6/us/news/none/article/other/mpu_factbox.html - -><script>adverts.addToArray({"pos":"mpu_factbox"})</script><span class="mol-ads-label-container"><span class="mol-ads-label">Advertisement</span></span>\n</div>\n</div></div></mol-permabox><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-bold"><span class="mol-style-medium">\xc2\xa0Top Trump aide Stephen Miller tests positive for COVID: Senior advisor becomes FIFTEENTH member of the President\'s inner circle to be infected after helping debate prep with Hope Hicks, Kellyanne Conway and Chris Christie</span></span></p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Stephen Miller, a senior policy adviser to President <a style="font-weight: bold;" href="/news/donald_trump/index.html" id="mol-a51125f0-085c-11eb-8f0e-c15f1938d0ff">Donald Trump</a>, has tested positive for <a style="font-weight: bold;" href="/news/coronavirus/index.html" id="mol-a51125f1-085c-11eb-8f0e-c15f1938d0ff">coronavirus</a>, an administration official says.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Miller, 35, tested positive for the virus on Tuesday after working remotely for the prior five days and testing negative every day through yesterday, according to NBC News reporter <a style="font-weight: bold;" class="class" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener" target="_blank" href="https://twitter.com/HallieJackson/status/1313611970655006721">Hallie Jackson</a>.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Miller is currently in quarantine. His wife, Katie Miller, tested positive for COVID-19 in May, but returned to work as Vice President Mike Pence\'s top spokeswoman after fully recovering from the infection at the time.\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0</p><div class="mol-img-group xwArtSplitter" style="style"> <div class="mol-img"> <div class="image-wrap"> <img id="i-880f4f5dd4c305bc" City.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">She is currently in Utah with the vice president\'s traveling party, an administration official told DailyMail.com.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">On Tuesday, White House physician Jesse Shonau said in a memo that Pence had tested negative for the virus earlier in the day.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">\'Vice President Mike Pence is encouraged to go about his normal activities and does not need to quarantine,\' the memo stated.\xc2\xa0</p><div class="moduleFull mol-video"><div><div itemprop="video" itemscope="itemscope" is now at least the 15th Trump aide to test positive for the virus. The president and first lady announced their positive result early on Friday, October 2.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Nearly all members of the White House \'cluster\' either attended a Rose Garden ceremony on September 26, or participated in debate prep with Trump ahead of the September 29 presidential debate.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Miller was a key participant in Trump\'s debate prep in the White House Map Room.</p><div class="mol-img-group xwArtSplitter" style="style"> <div class="mol-img"> <div class="image-wrap"> <img id="i-db811f71ffbbbbb9" 30</p></div><p class="mol-para-with-font">Also participating in the prep were\xc2\xa0Hicks, former New Jersey Governor Chris Christie, former counselor to the president Kellyanne Conway, and Trump campaign manager Bill Stepien, all of whom have tested positive for COVID-19 since the debate.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Miller, a top aide who has remained in his post since inauguration, is among the administration\'s most controversial figures.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">He is seen as the mastermind behind Trump\'s travel ban against several majority-Muslim countries, as well as the scuttled policy of arresting all people who entered the country illegally, resulting in the separation of children from family members.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">Miller\'s grandmother\xc2\xa0Ruth Glosser died at the age of 97 in July, with family members blaming coronavirus.</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">At the time, Miller denied that coronavirus was to blame for her death, telling <a style="font-weight: bold;" class="class" rel="nofollow noreferrer noopener" target="_blank" href="https://www.motherjones.com/politics/2020/07/stephen-millers-grandmother-died-of-covid-19-her-son-blames-the-trump-administration/?utm_source=twitter&amp;utm_campaign=naytev&amp;utm_medium=social">Mother Jones</a>\xc2\xa0through a spokesperson that Glosser had contracted the virus in March.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">\'She was diagnosed with COVID in March and passed away in July so that class="mol-factbox-title">TRUMP\'S INNER CIRCLE WHO HAVE TESTED POSITIVE FOR COVID</h3><div class="ins cleared mol-factbox-body"><p class="mol-para-with-font"><font color="#000000"><b><u>WEDNESDAY OCTOBER 1</u></b></font></p><div class="mol-img-group float-r mol-hidden-caption" style=""> <div class="mol-img"> <div class="image-wrap"> <img id="i-111895d2125196e0" It was not made public until after Trump\'s diagnosis.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font">She was last in contact with Trump on September 25.\xc2\xa0McDaniel began isolating on September 26 when a member of her family tested positive. She got her results several days later.\xc2\xa0</p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span class="mol-style-bold mol-style-underline">THURSDAY OCTOBER 2</span></p><p class="mol-para-with-font"><span
